Bro. Toppers crying over losing a single mark can be attributed to a combination of factors, including the intense pressure and expectations they face, a strong sense of identity tied to academic success, and the fear of failure or disappointing others.  Here's a more detailed breakdown: High Expectations: Toppers often experience significant pressure from parents, teachers, peers, and even themselves to maintain a high level of academic performance. This pressure can create a feeling that every mark lost is a personal failure or a deviation from their expected path.  Identity and Self-Worth: For some, academic success becomes a central part of their identity and self-worth. Losing even a single mark can trigger feelings of inadequacy or failure, as it can be perceived as a threat to their overall sense of self.  Fear of Disappointment: Toppers may worry about disappointing their parents, teachers, or other people in their lives if they don't maintain their high academic standing. The fear of not meeting expectations can lead to emotional distress when they experience a drop in marks.  Overwhelm and Stress: The constant pressure to perform well can lead to overwhelm and stress, making toppers more susceptible to emotional reactions, including crying, when they experience a setback.  Perfectionism: Some toppers may be perfectionists, striving for absolute accuracy in their studies and exams. Losing a single mark can feel like a significant deviation from their goal of perfection, leading to frustration and emotional distress.  Social Factors: The way that toppers are often treated and perceived in their social circles can also contribute to their emotional reactions. They may experience jealousy, pressure to maintain their status, or even feel isolated due to their academic success.  It's important to remember that while these feelings may seem extreme, they are a natural reaction to the intense pressure and expectations that many toppers experience. It's also important to acknowledge that emotional reactions can vary from person to person, and some may be more prone to emotional outbursts than others.

Honestly I feel bad for perfectionists and people who are pressured for 100%s, i myself get a bit irritated, even if for me its not a big deal, but its always annoyed me how some people can talk about it to people who got much lower scores. Like, dont make other people feel bad for not doing as well by acting like a 99 is bad, yknow? Its something I and other people in advanced math classes were taught pretty early(yes, im kind of bragging but tbf I dont do advanced math everyday just to not be able to brag a LITTLE). Which brings me to the topic of when other people lie about their own better scores or make them seem less good to cheer other people up. I think its good to remind your friends that youll be there for them if they need help, or that they can do better next time, or that its not the end of the world, but downplaying your own achievements doesnf really do that. To some people, it might feel condescending, especially if they find out you lied.
